item_32.note: Case: Estate-of-Betty-Prince-Premise-7-14-2020. Client: Estate of Betty Prince. The matter concerns Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Healthcare, and the deposition scheduling for Nurse Donna Jones as part of the Estate of Betty Prince Premise 7/14/2020 litigation, with the file maintained under the Filevine project account [EMAIL-722] and shared with multiple counsel.

In the email chain dated March through May 2025, counsel from The Whaley Law Firm and Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett (PPOA) coordinated depositions for this case. On March 18, 2025, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, emailed counsel to note that he had not been able to reach Ms. Donna Jones for potential deposition dates and to attach a proposed notice regarding the deposition of a corporate representative, asking recipients to review and provide dates as soon as possible. His message stated that the electronic communication was from The Whaley Law Firm and included his contact information and a standard attorney‑client privilege disclaimer.

Later that same day, Sarena M. Tuttle, the litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager for The Whaley Law Firm, replied that they had now received dates from Mrs. Donna Jones. Jones was available on May 2, May 6, or May 8, and Sarena asked which of those dates would work best for the opposing office and client.

Over the following weeks, multiple messages circulated among the parties. On March 18, 2025, Sarena reiterated that Donna Jones had provided availability for May 2, 6, or 8, and she asked counsel to confirm which dates would work. As part of deposition scheduling, The Whaley Law Firm’s Sarena M. Tuttle corresponded with opposing counsel and others to arrange depositions for Donna Jones, the nurse, and for Norton Healthcare’s corporate representative under Rule 30(b)(6).

Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, requested that Norton Healthcare identify the corporate representative to be deposed under 30(b)(6) and provide the representative’s name and available dates. In the matter of Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Healthcare, the parties engaged in a series of deposition scheduling communications. The Whaley Law Firm correspondence centers on scheduling depositions for a corporate representative under Rule 30(b)(6) and for a deposition of Ms. Donna Jones, a nurse whose availability was being coordinated with counsel for Norton Healthcare, as well as confirmation of dates from Norton Healthcare’s counsel.

The chain began with a December 3, 2024 email from Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, addressed to Ryan Nafziger of Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett, PLC, with a carbon copy list including Andrea Higgins; Joseph Effinger; Bryce Koon; Aaron Whaley; a Filevine project email address for Estate of Betty Prince Premise 7/14/2020; and Donna Jones. The subject was Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Healthcare - Deposition Scheduling. In the message, Sarena requested the name of Norton Healthcare’s corporate representative for a 30(b)(6) deposition and the dates that representative would be available for deposition. She provided contact details for her firm: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with D [PHONE-72], O [PHONE-700] ext 104, E Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, and noted the recipient’s new email address.

On December 5, 2024, Ryan Nafziger replied (subject line carried in the thread), asking whether a proposed CR 30.02(6) notice had been sent and requesting dates for the deposition of Donna Jones.

Jumping forward to March 18, 2025, Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm sent an email at 10:44 a.m. to counsel, explaining that Norton Healthcare had been unable to reach Ms. Jones for potential deposition dates and that they would like dates for Norton’s corporate representative as well. He attached a proposed notice for the 30(b)(6) deposition and asked counsel to review and provide deposition dates at their earliest convenience.

Later that same day, at 12:48 p.m., Sarena responded: they had now received dates from Mrs. Donna Jones, who was available on May 2, May 6, or May 8; she asked which of these dates would work best for counsel’s office and client.

Subsequently, on March 25, 2025 at 10:09 a.m., Sarena sent another message reiterating the request for availability for Donna Jones, noting that she was available on May 2, May 6, or May 8, and asking counsel to confirm whether any of these dates would work for their office and to schedule accordingly.

On March 27, 2025, at 1:34 p.m., Andrea Higgins, Legal Assistant to several Norton Healthcare defense attorneys (including Joseph M. Effinger, Esq.; Matthew A. Piekarski, Esq.; Ryan D. Nafziger, Esq.; and Michael J. Austin, Esq.), replied thanking for the apology and indicated that she would have Joe or Ryan contact the deposition scheduling directly regarding the deposition.

At 2:32 p.m. on March 27, 2025, Sarena replied to Andrea, apologizing for not being copied on the previous email chain regarding Donna Jones’ deposition scheduling and asking Andrea to confirm whether Mr. Nafziger and/or Mr. Effinger would be available on May 2, May 6, or May 8.

Later that same afternoon, at 2:55 p.m., Ryan Nafziger wrote: “Sarena, I am available May 6.” He noted this in the thread continuing the deposition scheduling discussion.

The thread also shows the broader context of the correspondence, including earlier communications from December 2024. On December 3, 2024, Sarena had initiated the request for a 30(b)(6) deposition of Norton Healthcare’s corporate representative and the dates available, and Ryan had replied on December 5, 2024, asking about the proposed CR 30.02(6) notice and requesting Donna Jones deposition dates. In sum, the parties engaged in a back-and-forth to schedule two depositions: (1) a corporate representative under 30(b)(6) for Norton Healthcare, and (2) Ms. Donna Jones, a nurse. The proposed dates for Ms. Jones were May 2, May 6, or May 8, 2025, with Norton HealthCare’s counsel indicating availability for May 6; counsel continued to coordinate with Ms. Jones’ availability and the counsel for Norton Healthcare, with communications spanning December 2024 through March 27, 2025.

Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, sent a message to Ryan Nafziger and Joseph Effinger, with copies to Bryce Koon, Aaron Whaley, an Estate of Betty Prince Filevine project email address, and Donna Jones. He attached a proposed notice regarding the corporate representative deposition and asked the recipients to review and provide dates for the corporate representative’s deposition at their earliest convenience. He noted that Donna Jones’s deposition dates were not yet confirmed beyond the May 2nd, 6th, or 8th options.

She stated that the dates provided on March 18, 2025—May 2, May 6, and May 8—had previously been communicated and noted that no response had yet been received. That same day, in the afternoon, Andrea Higgins, a legal assistant at Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett, PLC, responded on behalf of the Norton Healthcare side. In her email, she acknowledged the apology but indicated that Joe Effinger or Ryan Nafziger would be in direct contact regarding the deposition. The response was directed to Sarena Tuttle and included copies to Ryan Nafziger and Joseph Effinger, with additional CCs including Bryce Koon, Aaron Whaley, the Estate of Betty Prince Premise 7/14/2020 Filevine Project Email Address, and Donna Jones. Andrea’s signature reproduced her title and the firm’s contact information, along with the firm’s confidentiality disclaimer and contact details. The email reinforced that the deposition would be coordinated by the Norton Healthcare team rather than through a further chain of requests.

Throughout these communications, the matter consistently involved two deposition tracks: a 30(b)(6) deposition of Norton Healthcare’s corporate representative and the deposition of Nurse Donna Jones, with dates proposed for May 2, 6, or 8, 2025. The record also reflects standard confidentiality notices and routing details typical of law-firm correspondence, including the forwarding and copying to multiple counsel and related parties, and it references the Filevine project address used for the Estate of Betty Prince.

item_45.note: The Estate of Betty Prince is pursuing a case against Norton Healthcare, titled Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Healthcare, with the client identified as the Estate of Betty Prince. This note collects a series of email exchanges from late February to late March 2025 between the Whaley Law Firm, representing the estate, and Donna Jones of DSJ & Associates, regarding scheduling the deposition of Donna Jones in connection with the case. The correspondence repeatedly references the deposition dates May 2, May 6, and May 8, and notes that the deposition must occur before the scheduling order for trial is issued. The communications also mention that Donna Jones had previously reviewed medical records from Norton Health related to Betty Prince’s fall and subsequent passing, in October/November 2021, and that a statement from Donna was attached to one of the messages.

On February 24, 2025, Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm wrote to Mrs. Donna Jones, RN, at DSJ & Associates. She explained that Betty Prince’s case was approaching a trial date and that Donna’s deposition would need to be taken prior to the scheduling order. The message noted that Donna had previously reviewed Betty Prince’s medical records from Norton Health after her fall during a doctor visit, which contributed to the subsequent passing. A copy of Donna’s statement was attached for reference. Sarena requested dates in April when Donna would be available to complete the deposition.

A follow-up was sent on March 14, 2025, from Sarena to Donna Jones. The message stated, “Good afternoon Ms. Jones, We just wanted to follow up with you on our request for the best dates & times for your deposition. Please contact our office to discuss this in further detail.” The email included Sarena’s contact information and reiterated the firm’s request for available deposition dates.

On March 17, 2025, Donna Jones replied. She apologized for the delay and stated that her available dates included May 2, May 6, and May 8. She asked to be informed as soon as possible so she could place the deposition on her calendar. Donna also noted that the only records she had at that time were from Betty Prince’s Norton Health records; she requested that the Whaley firm forward any additional records to review, such as Norton’s policies and procedures or any depositions that had already been taken.

The following day, March 18, 2025, Sarena Tuttle responded. She explained that the dates Donna provided would be forwarded to the Defense Counsel to see which date works best for all parties, and that as soon as more information was available, she would reach out with a confirmation.

Later, on March 26, 2025, Donna Jones sent another message asking for a prompt determination. She reiterated the May 2, 6, and 8 dates and explained that she needed to adjust her April and May calendar due to other commitments. She added that if she could not obtain timely confirmation from the defense, she would not be able to commit to the deposition until sometime in June.

Finally, on March 27, 2025, Sarena Tuttle replied. She stated that she had already sent a follow-up to the defense and would send another one immediately, and that she would update Donna as soon as she heard back. She cautioned not to miss any commitments on their behalf and noted that if it became necessary to use the proposed May dates and push into June, they would work that out. She expressed appreciation for Donna’s assistance and did not intend to hinder her. Sarena signed the email with her position as Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm and included her new email address, Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, along with the firm’s Louisville, Kentucky office details.

The exchanges include standard confidentiality language typical of the communications, indicating that the messages contain privileged information for the addressees and should be kept confidential. The parties’ contact details appear in the signatures: Donna Jones’s information lists DSJ & Associates at 412 Hidden Lakes Lane, Brunswick, GA 31525, with the email [EMAIL-694], the website dsjandassociates.com, and the phone number [PHONE-80] (cell). Sarena Tuttle’s signature lists The Whaley Law Firm at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with the direct line [PHONE-692], the office line [PHONE-691] ext. 104, and the email Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (noting the new address). The case documents also reference the broader legal context, including the Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Healthcare and the anticipated setting of deposition dates ahead of a scheduling order governing the trial.

In sum, between February and March 2025, the Whaley Law Firm and Donna Jones coordinated deposition availability for Donna Jones, with May 2, May 6, and May 8 identified as potential dates, while balancing the need to forward proposed dates to defense counsel and to secure timely confirmations before the scheduling order is issued for the trial. The correspondence also highlights Donna’s prior involvement with Betty Prince’s Norton Health records and requests for any additional documents to inform the deposition review, all within the framework of standard confidential communications.

Re: Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Healthcare

This matter concerns the Estate of Betty Prince and its claim against Norton Healthcare. The following email communications between Donna Jones, RN, of DSJ & Associates, and Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager for The Whaley Law Firm, relate to scheduling Donna Jones’s deposition in connection with Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Healthcare.

On February 24, 2025, at 3:48 PM, Sarena Tuttle sent an email to Mrs. Jones explaining that in October/November of 2021, Mrs. Jones reviewed medical records for the referenced client after she fell during a Doctor visit at Norton Healthcare, an event that ultimately led to the client’s passing. Sarena noted that she attached a copy of Mrs. Jones’s statement for reference. She stated that, as the trial date approached, they would need to take Mrs. Jones’s deposition prior to the scheduling order being issued and asked Mrs. Jones to provide dates in April when she would be available for deposition.

In a follow-up, dated February 24, 2025, Sarena reiterated the request for April availability and attached Mrs. Jones’s statement for reference.

On Friday, March 14, 2025, at 2:49 PM, Sarena again wrote to Mrs. Jones, asking to follow up on the request for the best dates and times for the deposition and advised Mrs. Jones to contact the office to discuss the matter in further detail. The email was sent from The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with the firm’s contact details and a note indicating the recipient should contact the office to discuss scheduling.

On Monday, March 17, 2025, at 7:32 AM, Donna Jones replied. She apologised for the delay and stated that she was available on May 2, May 6, and May 8. She asked to be informed as soon as possible so she could put the deposition on her calendar. She also noted that the only records she possessed were Betty Prince’s records from Norton Health. If there were other records (e.g., Norton’s policies/procedures or any depositions taken), she requested that those be forwarded to her for review. Her message concluded with thanks and her standard sign-off, including her contact information for DSJ & Associates at 412 Hidden Lakes Lane, Brunswick, GA 31525, [EMAIL-83], and [PHONE-689] (cell). A confidentiality notice followed, stating that the message is intended only for the addressees and may contain privileged or confidential information; dissemination or use by anyone other than the addressee is prohibited, and recipients should destroy the message if they are not the intended recipient.

The next day, Tuesday, March 18, 2025, at 12:46 PM, Sarena responded to Mrs. Jones. She thanked Mrs. Jones and said they would forward the proposed dates to the Defense Counsel to determine which date works best for all parties. She added that as soon as there is more information, they would reach out with a confirmation. This message was sent from The Whaley Law Firm and carried the firm’s updated email address, along with the standard confidentiality disclaimer.

Earlier, on Friday, March 14, 2025, the prior note in the chain from Sarena (as described above) stated the request for the best deposition dates and times and asked Mrs. Jones to contact the office to discuss in further detail.

Finally, on Wednesday, March 26, 2025, at 19:56:21 +0000, Donna Jones sent a reply to Sarena. She requested that Sarena inform her as soon as possible whether any of the dates she had provided—May 2, May 6, and May 8—would work for the deposition. Donna explained she was organizing her calendar for April and May and had several other commitments being thrust upon her. She warned that if she could not obtain timely confirmation from the defense, she would not be able to commit to the deposition until sometime in June. Donna closed with thanks for prompt assistance and her customary sign-off, followed by her confidentiality disclaimer.

Donna Jones’s contact information appeared with her signature: Donna Jones, RN, DSJ & Associates, 412 Hidden Lakes Lane, Brunswick, GA 31525, [EMAIL-85], Dsjandassociates.com, [PHONE-687] (cell). The message also included the standard confidentiality notice indicating the message is intended only for the addressees, may contain privileged and confidential information, and that any use or dissemination by non-addressees is prohibited and should be destroyed or the sender advised.

In sum, the deposition scheduling communications between Donna Jones and Sarena Tuttle circulated from February 24, 2025 through March 26, 2025, with initial deposition date requests for April, subsequent discussions of May dates (May 2, 6, 8), updates about forwarding proposed dates to defense counsel for confirmation, and a final request for confirmation from Donna about whether any of the May dates would work, given her calendar constraints and the possibility of a June deposition if timely defense feedback could not be obtained. Each exchange included a standard confidentiality disclaimer typical of the parties’ communications.

item_50.note: The Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Healthcare is being handled by The Whaley Law Firm on behalf of the Estate of Betty Prince. The case file, labeled Estate-of-Betty-Prince-Premise-7-14-2020, involves deposition scheduling for Norton Healthcare, with Donna Jones (a nurse) and a Norton Healthcare corporate representative being discussed for depositions under 30(b)(6). The correspondence began in December 2024 and continued through March 2025, involving plaintiff counsel Sarena M. Tuttle and defense counsel W. Bryce Koon, among others.

On December 3, 2024, Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager for The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to Mr. Nafziger (and copied Bryce Koon and Aaron Whaley) requesting the deposition of Norton Healthcare’s Corporate Representative under Rule 30(b)(6). The message stated: “Good morning Mr. Nafziger, At this time, our office would like to take the deposition of a Corporate Representative of Norton Healthcare under 30(b)(6). Please provide the name of the representative and dates they are available to be deposed. If you have any questions, please do not hesitate to contact us directly to discuss them in further detail.” The email was sent from The Whaley Law Firm at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with D: [PHONE-90], O: [PHONE-91] ext 104, and E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (noting the new address).

Two days later, on December 5, 2024, Ryan Nafziger replied. He asked whether a proposed notice for the CR 30.02(6) deposition had been sent and requested dates for the deposition of Donna Jones as well. The message effectively sought a proposed notice for the corporate representative deposition and simultaneously requested scheduling information for Donna Jones.

On March 18, 2025, there were two separate exchanges. Bryce Koon, Esq., and the typical disclaimer block included in attorney communications.

Later that same day, at 12:48 p.m., Sarena Tuttle replied with an update: Norton Healthcare’s Corporate Representative deposition dates had now been received from Donna Jones. She stated that Ms. Jones was available on May 2, May 6, or May 8, and she asked which of these dates would work best for the office and the client. Her message again carried her signature block with The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information, and it included a note indicating that her email address had changed (Pleas note: “E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com” with the reminder about the new address).

Meanwhile, the initial thread shows an ongoing effort to coordinate with Norton Healthcare’s counsel. In the same March 18, 2025 timeframe, the original message from December 3, 2024 and the December 5, 2024 follow-up reflect the parties’ efforts to schedule the corporate deposition under 30(b)(6) and to obtain dates for Donna Jones’s deposition. The chain also documents that the March 18 messages included a standard attorney-client disclaimer in Bryce Koon’s email, underscoring the privileged nature of the communication.

Finally, on March 25, 2025, the latest note in the thread titled “Re: Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Healthcare - Deposition Scheduling” shows Sarena Tuttle following up with counsel. The message reiterates that Donna Jones had been identified as available on May 2, May 6, or May 8, 2025, but that the office had not yet received confirmation. It states: “Good morning Counselors, We just wanted to touch base on the dates for Nurse Donna Jones, last week we advised that she is available May 2nd, 6th or 8th, yet have not received a response. We are confident these dates will fill up soon if we are unable to get a confirmation over to her. Please confirm if any of these dates work for your office & schedule.” The email is signed by Sarena M. Tuttle with the same Whaley Law Firm contact details and again notes her new email address.

In sum, the deposition scheduling efforts in this matter have focused on securing dates for Donna Jones (Nurse Jones) on May 2, May 6, or May 8, 2025, while also pursuing dates for Norton Healthcare’s corporate representative under 30(b)(6). item_52.note: This note traces the exchange of emails regarding the Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Healthcare and the scheduling of Donna Jones, RN, of DSJ & Associates, as a witness for deposition.

In February 2025, The Whaley Law Firm’s Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager, reached out to Donna Jones, RN, of DSJ & Associates, about the Estate of Betty Prince. Tuttle reminded Jones that, in October or November 2021, Jones reviewed medical records for Betty Prince after she fell during a doctor visit at Norton Healthcare, an event that ultimately contributed to Prince’s passing. Tuttle stated that she had attached a copy of Jones’s statement for reference. With trial approaching, Tuttle explained that Jones’s deposition would need to be taken before the scheduling order was issued and asked Jones to provide dates in April when she would be available to testify. The Whaley Law Firm’s contact details listed for Tuttle were: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, D: [PHONE-677], O: [PHONE-676] ext 104, E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, noting the address of the new email address.

On February 24, 2025, Sarena Tuttle wrote again, this time with the subject Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Healthcare, to Donna Jones. In her message, she reiterated that Jones had reviewed the medical records related to Prince’s fall and death at Norton Healthcare in late 2021 and stated that a copy of Jones’s statement was attached. Tuttle reiterated the urgency due to the approaching trial date and again asked Jones to provide dates in April when she would be available to complete the deposition.

A separate exchange occurred on March 14, 2025. In an email to Donna Jones with the subject Re: Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Healthcare, Sarena Tuttle followed up to request the best dates and times for Jones’s deposition and asked Jones to contact the office to discuss the matter in further detail. Tuttle again provided her contact information and noted the new email address.

On March 17, 2025, Donna Jones responded. She apologized for the delay in replying and advised that her available dates for deposition were May 2, May 6, and May 8. She asked to be informed as soon as possible so she could place the deposition on the calendar. Jones also stated that the only records she possessed were Betty Prince’s records from Norton Health. If the recipient had additional records—such as Norton’s policies and procedures or any depositions taken—Jones requested that they be forwarded to her for review. She closed with thanks and respect, including her professional signature and contact information: Donna Jones, RN, DSJ & Associates, 412 Hidden Lakes Lane, Brunswick, GA 31525, [EMAIL-98], dsjandassociates.com, [PHONE-99] (cell). A standard confidentiality disclaimer followed, indicating the message was intended only for the addressees and that disclosure, use, or dissemination by others was prohibited, with instructions to destroy or delete the message and notify the sender if the recipient was not an intended addressee.

Overall, the thread shows a sequence of requests for deposition dates, with a focus on April availability initially requested, followed by Donna Jones’s later availability in early May, and a reminder to share any additional Norton Health records or depositions to aid Jones’s review.

She asked to be advised as soon as possible so she could put the deposition on the calendar. Donna also noted that the only records she currently possessed were Betty Prince’s Norton Health records, and she requested that if The Whaley Law Firm had additional records—such as Norton Health policies/procedures or any depositions—these be forwarded to her for review. Donna identified herself as Donna Jones, RN, of DSJ & Associates, with mailing address 412 Hidden Lakes Lane, Brunswick, GA 31525, and provided her email ([EMAIL-654]) and phone number [PHONE-653]). Her message included the standard confidentiality disclaimer typical of such communications.

This final note documented the ongoing coordination and confirmed that the new email address for Sarena was in use. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, prepared and circulated a series of discovery and filing communications beginning in late June 2024. The case file, designated Estate-of-Betty-Prince-Premise-7-14-2020, shows that the client is the Estate of Betty Prince.

On June 26, 2024, at 12:56 PM, Bryce Koon sent a message attaching correspondence related to the matter. The note included the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer common to electronic communications from the firm. The email flagged ongoing issues and served as a prelude to further discovery exchanges.

The next sequence of exchanges centers on the discovery dispute regarding Ms. Vinson’s training as a registration clerk. On July 9, 2024, at 4:21 PM, Koon wrote to Ryan Nafziger and Joseph Effinger (with a cc to the Estate of Betty Prince Premise 7/14/2020 – Filevine Project Email Address) noting that he recalled discussions by phone about the issues and that he had been under the impression a more detailed explanation of the objections would follow by email, but had not yet received it. He requested an update.

On July 10, 2024, at 10:25 AM, Ryan Nafziger replied that he was still looking into the policies discussed on the phone and could confirm that his client did not possess any security footage of the claimant. He explained that he was out of town for mediation for the next few days and would try to follow up soon with those policies. Bryce Koon responded at 10:26 AM, saying, “Sounds good. Thank you for getting back to me.” The email chain also included the standard privilege disclaimer.

Later on July 10, 2024, at 3:33 PM, Bryce Koon again reached out to Nafziger, expressing a desire to follow up on the issues and requesting an update.

On July 25, 2024, at 3:33 PM (as reflected in the chain), Bryce Koon sent another follow-up message to Nafziger requesting progress on the matter.

On July 31, 2024, at 12:53 PM, Nafziger responded that he was still working on the matter and was trying to ensure an accurate understanding of what training Ms. Vinson received while a registration clerk before formally answering the letter.

Then, on September 3, 2024, at 11:26 AM, Bryce Koon wrote again stating that he had not yet received any documents regarding Ms. Vinson’s training as a registration clerk or a response to the earlier letter. He warned that if the information was not provided promptly, he would be forced to file a motion to compel. This message also carried the firm’s privilege disclaimer.

Finally, on September 10, 2024, at 10:32:17 AM, Bryce Koon sent a message to counsel noting that the attached filing had been filed today in Jefferson Circuit Court and was set for Monday’s motion hour. The email included the same attorney-client privileged disclaimer and provided Bryce Koon’s contact information for The Whaley Law Firm at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with phone and fax numbers listed.

Throughout the thread, the participants were: Bryce Koon, Esq. (The Whaley Law Firm) as the sender in the estate matter; recipients included Ryan Nafziger and Joseph Effinger, with a cc to the Estate of Betty Prince Premise 7/14/2020 via a Filevine project email address. All emails carried the customary disclaimers regarding privilege and instructions if received in error.

In summary, the estate’s counsel pursued discovery related to Ms. Vinson’s training as a registration clerk, repeatedly requesting production of documents and clarification, while simultaneously filing and noting a matter set for motion in Jefferson Circuit Court on the pending docket of Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals, Inc.

Ryan replied later that day, stating he was still working on the matter and trying to ensure an accurate understanding of what training Ms. Vinsom (as he spelled it) received as a registration clerk before formally answering the letter.

Throughout the thread, the subject line consistently read: “Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals, Inc. (Jefferson 21-CI-003798).” The messages reflect an ongoing dispute over discovery related to Ms. Vinson’s training and related documents, with counsel pausing to gather and verify policies and any available training records before providing a formal response.

item_118.note: Case: Estate-of-Betty-Prince-Premise-7-14-2020. Client: the Estate of Betty Prince. This matter is styled Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals Inc. in Jefferson Circuit Court, case number 21-CI-003798.

The communications in this note arise from the estate’s discovery efforts in the above case and show a sequence of email correspondence between The Whaley Law Firm (attorney W. Bryce Koon, Esq.) and counsel for Norton Hospitals, with several recipients and CCs, between March and June of 2024. The Whaley Law Firm’s emails consistently carried their standard professional disclaimers about privilege and confidentiality.

On March 19, 2024, at 12:35 PM, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email to Ryan Nafziger (to [EMAIL-293]) and Joseph Effinger ([EMAIL-294]), with the [EMAIL-295] address CC’d. The subject was: “Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals Inc. (Jefferson Circuit 21-CI-003798).” In the body, Koon wrote: “Attached please find Plaintiff’s Supplemental Discovery Requests. If you need anything else from me in this regard, please let me know.” The signature included The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information: 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; Phone: [PHONE-477]; Fax: [PHONE-476]. A follow-up message was sent at 12:36 PM the same day stating: “Apologies – forgot to attach them!” with the same signature and confidentiality disclaimer.

On April 22, 2024, at 10:43 AM, Koon sent another message to [EMAIL-298] and [EMAIL-299], CC’ing [EMAIL-300], with the subject: “RE: Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals Inc. (Jefferson Circuit 21-CI-003798).” The body read: “Good afternoon counsel, Just writing to follow up on the below requests. Please advise when we may expect responses in this regard.” The message again carried The Whaley Law Firm’s standard contact details and confidentiality notice.

On April 30, 2024, at 11:00 AM, Koon emailed Ryan Nafziger and Joseph Effinger (CC’d to [EMAIL-301]) regarding the same matter, with the subject line unchanged. He wrote: “Good afternoon counsel, I am again writing to follow up on the outstanding discovery requests. If I do not hear from you by Thursday, I will be forced to file a motion to compel in this regard.” The email again included the firm’s address and contact information, along with the confidentiality disclaimer.

On May 2, 2024, at 9:44 AM, Ryan Nafziger replied to Bryce Koon (and CC’d Joseph Effinger, with Betty Prince’s file likely cc’d as well). Nafziger wrote: “Hi Bryce, Apologies for the late response. I am still waiting on some responsive information, but hope to have these to you by the end of next week.” This message also included the standard firm footer and confidentiality notice.

On June 3, 2024, at 9:35 AM, Nafziger sent another reply to Bryce Koon: “Bryce, Following our phone call last week, I just wanted to let you know that I am still hoping to provide our responses shortly – just waiting for a few more documents.” This communication appears in the thread that was later forwarded by Bryce Koon on June 3, 2024 at 10:10:43 AM, when he forwarded the email from Nafziger titled “RE: Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals Inc. (Jefferson Circuit 21-CI-003798).”

In sum, the notes document a back-and-forth about Plaintiff’s Supplemental Discovery Requests in the Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals Inc., including the initial attachment of the discovery requests on March 19, a correction that the attachments were forgotten, multiple follow-ups from The Whaley Law Firm seeking responses, and subsequent delays and expectations regarding production of responsive information. The correspondence consistently referenced the case caption and number (Jefferson Circuit 21-CI-003798), included Nahon Hospitals’ counsel’s email addresses ([EMAIL-302] and [EMAIL-303]), and CC’d the representative file address [EMAIL-304], with Joseph Effinger CC’d on several messages. The Whaley Law Firm’s communications also repeatedly contained their standard confidentiality and privilege notices.

item_128.note: In the case titled Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals Inc. (Jefferson Circuit Court, 21-CI-003798), the Estate of Betty Prince is represented by The Whaley Law Firm. The note documents a sequence of discovery communications between the firm and opposing counsel, spanning March through May 2024, with the matter tracked under the file Estate-of-Betty-Prince-Premise-7-14-2020.

On March 19, 2024, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email to opposing counsel at PPOA Law ([EMAIL-442] and [EMAIL-441]), with the subject Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals Inc. (Jefferson Circuit 21-CI-003798). In that message, he attached Plaintiff’s Supplemental Discovery Requests and cc’d the Estate’s Filevine portal address [EMAIL-440] and Sarena Tuttle. Shortly after, at 12:36 PM on the same day, Koon followed up with a separate email apologizing that the attachments had not been included. The emails each carried The Whaley Law Firm’s standard confidentiality disclaimer, noting that the messages are intended only for the named recipient and that, if received in error, the recipient should contact the firm and not disclose or use privileged information.

A little over a month later, on April 22, 2024, Koon again wrote to opposing counsel (to the same recipients, rnafziger and jeffinger, with the same subject line) to follow up on the requests. In that message, he stated, “Good afternoon counsel, Just writing to follow up on the below requests. Please advise when we may expect responses in this regard,” and he again signed as W. Bryce Koon, Esq., The Whaley Law Firm, with the firm’s Louisville, Kentucky address (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222) and contact information (Phone: [PHONE-334]; Fax: [PHONE-335]). The message reiterated the standard attorney-client confidentiality notice.

On April 30, 2024, Koon sent another follow-up regarding the outstanding discovery requests. He wrote, “Good afternoon counsel, I am again writing to follow up on the outstanding discovery requests. If I do not hear from you by Thursday, I will be forced to file a motion to compel in this regard.” This email also carried the Whaley Law Firm signature block and confidentiality notice.

The following day, May 2, 2024, Ryan Nafziger of PPOA Law replied to Bryce Koon. In his reply, Nafziger apologized for the late response, explained that he was still waiting on some responsive information, and stated that he hoped to have the information to Bryce by the end of the next week. Nafziger closed his message with a brief thank you. The thread continued with the standard email formatting and the confidentiality disclaimer included in the outgoing communications.

In summary, this note tracks a persistent discovery dispute in Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals Inc., with plaintiff’s counsel repeatedly requesting discovery responses, issuing warnings of a potential motion to compel if no timely reply, and opposing counsel replying on May 2, 2024, indicating that responsive information was still being gathered and would be provided by the end of the following week. The communications include multiple CCs to the Estate’s Filevine portal and to Sarena Tuttle, and all messages incorporate the Whaley Law Firm’s contact details and privilege notices.

item_150.note: Case: Estate-of-Betty-Prince-Premise-7-14-2020. Client: Estate of Betty Prince. This file concerns the Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals, docket number 21-CI-003798, in which the plaintiff is the Estate of Betty Prince.

Between October 16 and October 25, 2023, a series of email communications took place between counsel representing the Estate and counsel for Norton Hospitals regarding discovery and a protective order, with documents and records to be produced under that order. On Monday, October 16, 2023, at 3:01 p.m., Blake Gerstner of Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett, PLC wrote to Bryce Koons of The Whaley Law Firm. He apologized for the delay and stated that attached please be found the defendant’s discovery responses. He said they would forward a OneDrive link the next day containing the referenced medical records and bills, as well as a signed verification page, and that once the Agreed Protective Order had been entered they would forward the applicable documents. He concluded by inviting any questions or concerns, and his email included the customary confidentiality notice.

Later the same afternoon, at 3:08 p.m., Bryce Koon responded: “Thank you for getting back to me. You may sign on our behalf.” He signed off with his contact information for The Whaley Law Firm, including his Louisville address at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, phone and fax numbers, and his electronic signature block. The message also contained the firm’s standard confidentiality disclaimer.

Earlier that day, at 3:01 p.m., Blake had also noted in a separate message that they were in receipt of the outstanding discovery responses, had been diligently working on them, and would have the responses by the end of the day. He reiterated that some documents were confidential and reiterated the preference that Bryce execute the attached Agreed Protective Order to protect their client’s interests; he added that if Bryce could not agree to the proposed order, they would still produce the documents with an agreement to keep them confidential while the Protective Order was litigated. This message also carried the firm’s confidentiality notice.

At 5:06 p.m. on October 16, 2023, Blake sent another message reiterating that they had received the request for discovery responses and that they would have them by the end of the day. He explained that some of the documents were confidential and that they would prefer Bryce to execute the attached Agreed Protective Order; he also offered to e-sign for Bryce with permission. He confirmed that they had been diligently working on the responses and that once the Agreed Protective Order had been entered, they would forward the applicable documents. The email again included Blake’s signature block and the firm’s confidentiality notice.

More than a week later, on Monday, October 16, 2023, at 3:01 p.m., Blake sent another message in the thread indicating that the parties were awaiting the protective order’s entry and that the documents to be produced were confidential, with a proposed protective order to govern access. The tone throughout this sequence was to secure a protective order before sharing the confidential materials.

On Wednesday, October 25, 2023, at 10:01 a.m., Blake Gerstner again wrote to Bryce Koons regarding the same Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals matter. He apologized for the delay and attached the documents referenced in his previous email, produced pursuant to the agreed protective order, along with a one-drive link containing the Plaintiff’s medical and billing records. He asked Bryce to review and to contact him if there were questions or concerns. The body of this email included the standard signature for Blake Gerstner, Associate Attorney, Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett, PLC, with the firm’s Louisville address (716 West Main Street, Suite 300, Louisville, KY 40202), telephone and fax numbers, and the website w ppoalaw.com. It also included the firm’s confidentiality notice.

The emails also show the broader context of the correspondence, including the presence of standard confidentiality language in each message and the logistical details of production under the protective order. The subject line on these communications consistently read: “Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals (21-CI-003798).” The October 25 exchange was forwarded within the team: Bryce Koon forwarded Blake’s October 25 message as “FW: Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals (21-CI-003798)” to Sarena Tuttle at sarena@whaleylawfirm.com, with a cc to [EMAIL-404], dated October 25, 2023, 10:37:03 -0400.

Attachments and materials referenced across the chain included documents produced under the Agreed Protective Order, along with a one-drive link containing the Plaintiff’s medical and billing records, and, in one message, a signed verification page. The communications also recorded the ongoing use of a protective order to govern the sharing and handling of confidential information, with the expectation that the protective order would be entered before full production of the documents.

In summary, the record reflects a coordinated discovery process in the Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals, centered on compliance with an Agreed Protective Order, the production of defendant discovery responses, and the provision of medical and billing records via a one-drive link to the plaintiff’s counsel, all within a sequence of dated emails from October 16 through October 25, 2023, including professional signatures and confidentiality notices typical of this practice.

item_163.note: Case: Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals, 21-CI-003798. The client is the Estate of Betty Prince. The correspondence centers on scheduling depositions of two potential witnesses: Norton employee Lucretia Vinsom and Mr. Robert Prince (the latter described as retired with open availability). The exchanges spanned December 2023 through January 2024 and involved counsel from The Whaley Law Firm (Bryce W. Koon, Esq.; Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal & Workers’ Compensation Case Manager) and counsel from PPOA Law (Ryan Nafziger, Esq.; Joseph Effinger, Esq.; Andrea Higgins, Esq.), with the Whaley firm’s contact details and the PPOA firm’s contact details listed in the signatures. The messages also included standard attorney-client privilege disclosures in every electronic transmission, and Sarena Tuttle noted a new email address in her signature.

The discussion began on December 7, 2023, when Bryce Koon asked whether Norton employee Lucretia Vinsom remained with Norton and requested potential deposition dates. On December 11, 2023, Ryan Nafziger replied that Ms. Vinsom was still a Norton employee and that he would check with her to obtain deposition dates; he also indicated an interest in deposing Mr. Robert Prince if dates could be found. The following day, December 12, 2023, Sarena Tuttle responded that Mr. Prince is retired and has open availability, with no standing appointment to work around, and requested dates for deposing Mr. Prince.

Further scheduling back-and-forth continued through December 2023. On December 26, 2023, Bryce again asked for potential dates for Ms. Vinsom’s deposition, and on December 29, 2023, Ryan noted he was still working on obtaining dates and would respond the following week, wishing everyone a Happy New Year. By December 12, 2023, Sarena had already indicated that Mr. Prince’s deposition could be scheduled given his retirement and available windows.

In early January 2024, the parties narrowed the window for Ms. Vinsom’s deposition. On January 8, 2024, Ryan stated that Ms. Vinsom was available January 29, 30 and February 1, 2 and February 5–9, with a week of February 12–16 unavailable but the witness could be available afterward; he suggested arranging both depositions on the same day and hosting at his office. Bryce Koon replied later that day, asking for progress on securing dates for Ms. Vinsom’s deposition. Ryan reaffirmed Ms. Vinsom’s availability and again offered to host at his office, asking whether any of the listed dates would work for the client and whether both depositions could be done on the same day.

On January 9, 2024, Bryce indicated that Tuesday, February 6 would work best for all involved. Ryan then sought preference on the time for the day, proposing the first deposition at 10:00 a.m. and the second at noon or thereafter. The following day, January 10, 2024, Sarena replied that starting the day at 10:00 a.m. was perfect for their office and provided her contact information, including a new email address (Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com) and the firm’s full contact details. The message also carried the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer.

In summary, the parties settled on scheduling two depositions for Tuesday, February 6, 2024, with the planned sequence to begin at 10:00 a.m. for the first deposition and the second at 12:00 p.m. or later, to be conducted on the same day at Ryan Nafziger’s office, pending confirmations of Ms. Vinsom’s and Mr. Prince’s availabilities. The correspondence repeatedly confirms Ms. Vinsom’s status as a Norton employee and Mr. Prince’s retirement with open availability, and all communications include the customary privilege notices and firm signatures.

item_166.note: Case: Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals (21-CI-003798). Client: Estate of Betty Prince.

In the binders for the Estate of Betty Prince, counsel began a series of email exchanges in December 2023 and January 2024 concerning depositions of two Norton witnesses in the matter. The first request, dated December 7, 2023, came from W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm. He asked whether Norton employee Lucretia Vinsom, identified in the Safety and Security Report produced in discovery, would be available for deposition and requested potential dates for scheduling her deposition.

On December 11, 2023, Ryan Nafziger replied that Ms. Vinsom is apparently still a Norton employee and that he would check with her to obtain deposition dates. He also indicated a desire to request the deposition of Mr. Robert Prince, asking Bryce Koon to check with Mr. Prince for possible dates.

The following day, December 12, 2023, Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, responded. She stated that Mr. Prince is retired and has open availability, and that he currently does not have any standing appointments to work around. She advised sending dates for Mr. Prince’s deposition.

Later in December, on December 26, 2023, Bryce Koon asked whether there were any potential dates yet for Ms. Vinsom’s deposition. Ryan Nafziger did not provide dates at that time but indicated on December 29, 2023, that he was still working on obtaining dates and would follow up the next week, wishing everyone a Happy New Year.

As January 2024 began, Ryan provided a concrete window for Ms. Vinsom’s deposition. On January 8, 2024, he informed Bryce that Ms. Vinsom was available January 29, 30 and February 1, 2 and 5–9. He noted that she would be unavailable the week of February 12–16, but could be available afterward if those dates did not work. He offered to host the depositions at his office and suggested that both depositions could be completed on the same day.

Bryce followed up the same day, January 8, 2024, asking whether any progress had been made on scheduling Ms. Vinsom’s deposition.

In subsequent exchanges on January 9, 2024, the parties refined the plan. Ryan noted that February 6 would be the date and asked for a preferred time, proposing the first deposition at 10:00 and the second at noon or thereafter. Bryce confirmed that Tuesday, February 6 would work best for all involved. He included the Whaley Law Firm’s contact details and a standard attorney-client privilege notice commonly attached to emails. The Whaley Law Firm’s address listed was 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with a phone number of [PHONE-469] and a fax number of [PHONE-470]. The communications also carried the customary disclaimer about privileged information and the instruction to contact the firm if the message was received in error.

Earlier in the thread, Bryce’s December 7, 2023 request to depose Lucretia Vinsom had sought dates for her deposition, and Ryan’s December 11, 2023 reply confirmed his belief that she remained a Norton employee and that he would check with her about deposition dates, while also noting an interest in deposing Mr. Prince if possible. By December 12, 2023, Sarena Tuttle had clarified that Mr. Prince was retired but available, and instructed the team to propose dates for his deposition. The communications reflect Ryan Nafziger’s role in coordinating depositions and hosting arrangements, while Bryce Koon and Sarena Tuttle interacted with respect to who would be deposed and when.

Across these communications, the objective remained clear: schedule two depositions—one for Lucretia Vinsom and one for Mr. Robert Prince—on a single day to be determined, with February 6, 2024 as the proposed date, and to commence with the first deposition at 10:00 and the second at 12:00 or thereafter, with the depositions to be hosted at Ryan Nafziger’s office if feasible. The notes also reflect the evolving availability: Ms. Vinsom’s availability windows (January 29, 30; February 1, 2; and February 5–9) and her unavailability the week of February 12–16, and Mr. Prince’s status as retired with open schedules.

For completeness, the communications include standard attorney-client privilege notices and new email address references for Sarena Tuttle, who signs as Litigation Paralegal & Workers’ Compensation Case Manager for The Whaley Law Firm.

item_171.note: In the Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals, docket number 21-CI-003798, the Estate of Betty Prince (the client) and The Whaley Law Firm were coordinating depositions related to the case. The communications, occurring between December 2023 and February 2024, sought to schedule depositions of two witnesses: Norton employee Lucretia Vinsom and Mr. Robert Prince (the decedent’s father). The principal participants were W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, and counsel for Norton Hospitals, including Ryan Nafziger and litigation paralegal Sarena M. Tuttle. (Sarena’s signature notes a new email address, and the signature block for Bryce includes the Whaley firm’s Louisville address and contact numbers.)

The scheduling effort began on December 7, 2023, when Bryce Koon asked whether Norton employee Lucretia Vinsom could be deposed, noting that Vinsom was identified in the Safety and Security Report provided in Norton’s discovery production, and requesting potential deposition dates if she remained with Norton. In reply on December 11, 2023, Ryan Nafziger indicated his understanding that Ms. Vinsom was still a Norton employee and that he was checking with her to obtain deposition dates; he also expressed a desire to request Mr. Robert Prince’s deposition if dates could be found. On December 12, 2023, Sarena Tuttle, Norton’s litigation paralegal, replied that Mr. Prince was retired and had open availability, with no standing appointment to work around, and she asked that dates be provided for deposing Mr. Prince.

Bryce followed up on December 26, 2023, asking for potential dates for Lucretia Vinsom’s deposition. On December 29, 2023, Nafziger replied that he was still working on obtaining dates and would get back next week, and he wished everyone a happy new year. The same day, Bryce had earlier communications with the group regarding the search for dates, including availability inquiries for Ms. Vinsom.

In early January 2024, Nafziger provided an update on Ms. Vinsom’s availability: she was available January 29 and 30, and February 1, 2, and 5–9; she would be unavailable the week of February 12–16, but could be scheduled after that if needed. Nafziger noted that he could host the depositions at his office and that they could potentially be scheduled on the same day for both witnesses. Bryce responded on January 8, 2024, asking whether progress had been made on obtaining dates for Ms. Vinsom’s deposition. A follow-up exchange occurred on January 9, 2024, when Bryce wrote that he had spoken with Mr. Prince and that Tuesday, February 6 would work best for all parties. He closed with his customary contact information.

Thus, the record reflects a coordinated effort across December 2023 and early January 2024 to schedule depositions of Lucretia Vinsom and Mr. Robert Prince, with the parties ultimately aiming to conduct both depositions on a single day (Tuesday, February 6, 2024) at the office of the plaintiffs’ counsel, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, in Louisville, Kentucky.

item_174.note: Case: Estate-of-Betty-Prince-Premise-7-14-2020. Client: Estate of Betty Prince. This note concerns the Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals (case number 21-CI-003798). The correspondence below reflects efforts by counsel for the Estate to schedule depositions in the Norton Hospitals matter, specifically deposition dates for Norton employee Lucretia Vinsom, as identified in Norton’s discovery materials, and a potential deposition of Mr. Robert Prince.

On December 7, 2023, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to counsel at PPOA and to Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm, requesting potential deposition dates for Norton employee Lucretia Vinsom, who is identified in the Safety and Security Report included in the discovery production. He asked to confirm whether Ms. Vinsom remains a Norton employee and to provide dates for her deposition.

On December 11, 2023, Ryan Nafziger replied that Ms. Vinsom is still a Norton employee and that he was checking with her to obtain deposition dates. He also stated an interest in requesting Mr. Robert Prince’s deposition if dates could be arranged.

On December 12, 2023, Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager for The Whaley Law Firm, replied. She stated that Mr. Prince is retired and has open availability, with no standing appointment to contend with. She asked that the offices send dates for deposing Mr. Prince.

On December 7, 2023, in a separate thread, Bryce Koon had also asked whether Norton employee Lucretia Vinsom could be deposed and requested potential dates for that deposition, referencing Vinsom’s identification in the Safety and Security Report.

In December 2023, counsel from The Whaley Law Firm coordinated deposition dates in the case Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals (21-CI-003798). The exchanges center on whether Norton employee Lucretia Vinsom may be deposed and on scheduling a deposition for Mr. Robert Prince, the latter being referenced as Mr. Prince in the emails. The correspondence involves W. Bryce Koon, Esq., the Whaley Law Firm, and colleagues including Sarena M. Tuttle, Ryan Nafziger, Blake Gerstner, Joseph Effinger, Andrea Higgins, and Aaron Whaley. The note set captures four email communications, spanning December 7, 11, 12, and 26, 2023, with standard confidentiality and privilege notices included in each message.

On December 7, 2023, at 3:50 PM, Bryce Koon sent the initial request. He asked counsel to confirm whether Norton employee Lucretia Vinsom, identified in the Safety and Security Report provided in the opposing party’s discovery production, is still employed by Norton and, if so, to provide potential deposition dates. His message concluded with his contact information: W. Bryce Koon, Esq., The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, phone [PHONE-485], fax [PHONE-486]. The email included the customary attorney-client privileged disclaimer indicating the message is intended only for the named recipient and outlining the precautionary steps if received in error.

Three days later, on December 11, 2023, at 4:48 PM, Ryan Nafziger replied. He indicated his understanding that Ms. Vinsom remained a Norton employee and that he was checking with her to obtain deposition dates. He also stated an additional desire to request Mr. Robert Prince’s deposition if Bryce Koon could check with him for dates. This message was addressed to Bryce Koon, with copies to Blake Gerstner and Joseph Effinger, Andrea Higgins, and Sarena Tuttle, and it carried the same standard confidentiality disclaimer.

On December 12, 2023, at 10:08 AM, Sarena Tuttle responded to Nafziger. She informed him that Mr. Prince is retired and has open availability, and she noted that they had confirmed Mr. Prince currently does not have any standing appointment to work around. She requested that Nafziger’s office provide dates for deposing Mr. Prince. This reply was sent to Ryan Nafziger with copies to Bryce Koon, Blake Gerstner, Joseph Effinger, Andrea Higgins, and Aaron Whaley, and she also included a note that Mr. Prince’s information reflects a new email address for the sender. The message ended with the Whaley Law Firm’s standard disclaimer about confidentiality and privilege.

Finally, on December 26, 2023, at 3:15 PM (−0500), Bryce Koon followed up with the group. He asked, “Do we have any potential dates yet for Ms. Vinsom’s deposition?” The email was sent to the same recipients listed in the first message, with the Whaley Law Firm’s confidentially disclaimer included.

Across these communications, the core issues being pursued were (1) whether Norton employee Lucretia Vinsom is currently employed and available for deposition, with counsel seeking potential deposition dates, and (2) whether Mr. Robert Prince—described as retired and with open availability—could be deposed, with the opposing side asked to propose dates. The exchanges also record the evolving understanding of Mr. Prince’s status (retired with no standing work commitments) and the ongoing effort to coordinate deposition scheduling, all within the case captioned Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals (21-CI-003798). The messages consistently include the standard attorney-client privilege/confidentiality notices.

The envelope number associated with this filing is 6752697, and the case caption reads Prince, Robert vs. Norton Hospitals, Inc. The filing was submitted by the eFiler Blake Anthony Gerstner, who is attorney for the defendant. The court identified the proceeding as Jefferson Circuit (Circuit Court), and the docket is listed under Case Number 21-CI-003798. The notice confirms there were no scheduled events at that time.

The circuit clerk’s processing occurred on October 18, 2023, at 3:45 PM Eastern. The notice was electronically mailed to the following recipients: Aaron Gregory Whaley ([EMAIL-513]); Matthew Piekarski ([EMAIL-514]); Joseph Effinger ([EMAIL-515]); Ryan Nafziger ([EMAIL-516]); and Blake Anthony Gerstner ([EMAIL-517]).

The notice states that it was automatically generated by the Kentucky Court of Justice eFiling system and that recipients should not reply to the email.

item_199.note: Case: Estate of Betty Prince, Estate-of-Betty-Prince-Premise-7-14-2020. The client is the Estate of Betty Prince, in the matter Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals, docket number 21-CI-003798.

On October 16, 2023, at 3:01 PM, Blake Gerstner of Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett, PLC, wrote to W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, regarding the Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospitals. In his email, he stated that they were in receipt of Koon’s message concerning the outstanding discovery responses, and that they had been diligently working on them and would have the responses by the end of the day. He noted that some of the documents to be produced are confidential and that they would prefer Koon execute the attached Agreed Protective Order to protect their client’s interests in the information, adding that he was also happy to e-sign for Koon “with permission.” He warned that if Koon could not agree to the proposed order, they would produce the documents with Koon’s agreement to keep them confidential as the Protective Order litigation proceeded. He concluded by inviting any questions or concerns. The email carried the signature of Blake Gerstner, Associate Attorney, and included the firm’s contact information: Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett, PLC, 716 West Main Street, Suite 300, Louisville, Kentucky 40202; telephone [PHONE-546]; fax [PHONE-547]; website w ppoalaw.com. A confidentiality disclaimer followed, noting that the message from the law firm is for the sole use of the intended recipient and may contain confidential and privileged information; it advised against copying or forwarding to unauthorized persons, and instructed the recipient to contact the sender to report an error and to destroy all copies if not the intended recipient.

Earlier that same day, at 3:08 PM, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., appended a response from The Whaley Law Firm to Blake Gerstner. In that message, Koon thanked Gerstner for getting back to him and indicated, “You may sign on our behalf.” The email included Koon’s firm contact details: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-548]; fax [PHONE-549]. It also contained a standard confidentiality notice stating that the electronic message is intended only for the named recipient and may contain attorney-client privileged or otherwise protected information; if the message or any attachment were received in error, the recipient was instructed to contact The Whaley Law Firm, advise of the error, and note that no waiver of privilege shall be applicable, and that the recipient should not use or forward the information to any third party not intended to receive it. The message also reiterated the sender’s role and provided the signature block for W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm.

item_211.note: In the estate case titled Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospital, Inc. ( Jefferson Circuit 21-CI-003798 ), the Estate of Betty Prince is the client. The case involved ongoing discovery disputes, and a chain of email communications from August through September 2023 shows the efforts of counsel for the estate to obtain responses, schedule depositions, and identify an individual referenced in discovery.

On August 17, 2023, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, emailed the opposing counsel (Ryan Nafziger and Joseph Effinger) noting that while responses to the Requests for Admission had been received, there did not appear to be responses to the Interrogatories or the Document Requests. He said a letter had been sent a few weeks prior and asked for guidance on when the remaining discovery responses would be provided.

Several days later, on August 22, 2023, Koon sent two emails. In the first, at 2:32 p.m., he stated that he had not heard back regarding his previous email and that it had been an inordinate amount of time since the requests were propounded; he warned that if responses were not received very soon, he would be forced to file a Motion to Compel. He also asked whether the individual referenced in the attached document could be identified. Later that same day, at 2:46 p.m., Nafziger replied that he was in the process of completing the discovery and would have the materials to Koon by the end of the following week; Nafziger also recalled prior experience of nearly a year and a half of emailing to obtain complete responses and thanked Koon for his patience. The exchange included reference to a file or link titled BettyPrinceSFZ954585.

Also on August 22, 2023, there was a second message from Koon to Nafziger and Effinger (with BettyPrinceSFZ954585 in copy) indicating that he would continue to work toward obtaining the discovery responses, while acknowledging the ongoing effort required.

On August 28, 2023, Koon emailed again, indicating that the opposing side could have additional time to provide the discovery responses if needed. He also asked to proceed with scheduling the deposition of the individual identified in the attached document. He noted that the person’s name was not known, only initials “LV,” and he requested identification of that individual along with potential deposition dates.

On September 15, 2023, Koon followed up by asking when the discovery responses could be expected and whether the individual referenced earlier could be identified.

Finally, on September 22, 2023, Koon wrote that he had not heard back regarding the outstanding discovery responses and that he needed the client’s answers by Wednesday, September 27, 2023. He warned that if the responses were not provided by that date, he would be forced to file the attached motion. The message reiterated the same contact information and included the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer common to The Whaley Law Firm emails, which states that the message is intended only for the named recipient and may contain privileged information; if received in error, the recipient should contact The Whaley Law Firm, avoid waiving any privilege, and not use the information or forward it to anyone not intended to receive it.

Across the sequence, the emails repeatedly documented the pursuit of discovery responses to Interrogatories and Document Requests, the status of Responses to Requests for Admission (which had been received), the attempt to identify the individual referenced by initials (LV), and the scheduling of a deposition, all while noting the need to preserve privilege and confidentiality through standard email notices. The communications reflect a persistent effort by the Estate of Betty Prince’s counsel to move the discovery process forward and to enforce timely responses under the court’s expectations.

item_213.note: In the Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Hospital, Inc., Jefferson Circuit Court case 21-CI-003798, discovery has been the subject of ongoing correspondence between the Estate’s counsel and opposing counsel. The case is titled Estate of Betty Prince, with the client listed as the Estate of Betty Prince, and the case file reference includes Estate-of-Betty-Prince-Premise-7-14-2020. The communications flow from mid-August through September 2023 and involve the discovery schedule for Interrogatories, Documents requests, and Requests for Admission, as well as a deposition relevant to an identified individual.

On August 17, 2023, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email to opposing counsel ([EMAIL-585] and [EMAIL-586], cc’ing [EMAIL-587]). He noted that the defendants’ Responses for Admission had been received earlier, but no answers had been provided to the Interrogatories or the Document Requests. He indicated that he had emailed a letter a few weeks prior on the matter and asked for an advisory on when answers could be expected. The message included the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer.

Two days later, on August 22, 2023, Bryce Koon sent two separate messages. At 2:32 PM, he again pressed that he had not heard back regarding his previous email and letter. He stated that it had been an inordinate amount of time since the discovery requests were propounded and that no responses had been received to date. He warned that if responses were not forthcoming very soon, he would be forced to file a Motion to Compel. The email carried the same attorney-client privilege disclaimer and contact details for The Whaley Law Firm.

Shortly thereafter, at 2:46 PM the same day, Ryan Nafziger replied. He said he was in the process of completing the discovery requests and would have them to Bryce Koon by the end of the following week. He recalled that it had previously taken almost a year and a-half of emailing to obtain complete responses to their requests and thanked Bryce for his patience. This message also included the standard privilege disclaimer and the familiar contact information for the parties.

On August 28, 2023, Bryce Koon replied to Nafziger and Effinger. He indicated that they were certainly willing to grant additional time for the responses. He asked to proceed with scheduling the deposition for the individual identified in an attached document. He noted that the only information available about this individual appeared to be initials “LV,” and that the name itself was not provided. He requested identification of the individual and suggested providing potential deposition dates. The communication again carried the standard privilege disclaimer and the Whaley Law Firm contact details.

Finally, on September 15, 2023, Bryce Koon sent a follow-up email to Ryan Nafziger and Joseph Effinger, with the subject Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospital, Inc. (Jefferson Circuit 21-CI-003798) - Discovery. He wrote in the body: Good afternoon counsel, it has been a few weeks since their previous discussions. He asked when they could expect responses to the discovery requests and whether the opposing side had identified the individual previously referenced. He signed as W. Bryce Koon, Esq., The Whaley Law Firm, with the firm’s Louisville address, telephone, and fax numbers, and again included the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer.

Across all exchanges, the emails repeatedly included standard disclaimers stating the message was intended only for the named recipient and could contain attorney-client privileged or protected information; if received in error, the recipient was instructed to contact The Whaley Law Firm and not to disclose or forward the contents. The correspondences also reflect the ongoing effort to resolve discovery responses, to schedule the deposition for the individual identified only by initials LV, and to obtain clarity on the identity of that person, all within the procedural context of the Estate of Betty Prince v Norton Hospital, Inc.

The subject line was Estate of Betty Prince v. Norton Hospital, Inc. (Jefferson Circuit 21-CI-003798) - Discovery. In the message, Koon stated that they were willing to grant the opposing side additional time to respond to discovery requests but wanted to set the matter on their radar. He also asked to begin scheduling the deposition of an individual referenced in an attached document. The name of this individual was not provided in the email, only the initials “LV.” Koon requested that the recipients identify the person corresponding to those initials and provide several potential deposition dates. He concluded by thanking them and providing his contact information. The message included the standard confidentiality disclaimer common to attorney communications, noting that the electronic message is intended only for the named recipient and may contain attorney-client privileged or otherwise protected information; if received in error, the recipient should contact The Whaley Law Firm and not disclose or forward the information.

The exchange also included prior communications from the same two attorneys, dating earlier in August 2023.

On August 22, 2023, at 2:46 p.m., Ryan Nafziger replied to Bryce Koon (and Joseph Effinger) with a cc to [EMAIL-593]. Nafziger wrote that he was in the process of completing the discovery responses and expected to have them to Koon by the end of the following week. He added that, as he recalled, it had taken nearly a year and a half of emailing to obtain complete responses to their requests, and he appreciated Koon’s patience.

Also on August 22, 2023, at 2:32 p.m., Bryce Koon sent another message to Nafziger and Effinger (cc’ing [EMAIL-594]). In this message, Koon stated that he had not heard back regarding a previous email and letter. He emphasized that it had been an inordinately long time since the discovery requests were propounded and that no responses had been received to date. He warned that if responses were not provided very soon, he would be forced to file a Motion to Compel. He asked for a response.

Earlier still, on August 17, 2023, at 10:52 a.m., Koon wrote to [EMAIL-595] and [EMAIL-596] (cc’ing [EMAIL-597]). He observed that they had received responses to their Requests for Admission some time earlier, but the emails indicated that there had been no responses to Interrogatories or document requests. He noted that he had sent a letter a few weeks prior and had received no response. He asked when they could expect answers to these discovery requests.

In summary, the estate’s counsel faced delayed discovery responses in the Norton Hospital case and sought confirmation of the identity of the deposition subject identified only by initials LV, along with proposed deposition dates. They also communicated a willingness to allow additional time for discovery responses but pressed for timely responses or the possibility of a Motion to Compel if such responses were not forthcoming. The timeline shows a pattern of repeated requests and responses across mid-to-late August 2023, with the most recent August 28 message seeking to move forward with scheduling and identifying the LV individual.

Norton Hospital, focused on the Plaintiff’s responses to discovery requests and the processing of medical and social security authorizations.

On Friday, July 21, 2023, at 11:23 AM, Sarena Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager for The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email to Andrea Higgins of Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett, PLC, with copies to Matthew Piekarski, Joseph Effinger, and Ryan Nafziger, and with Aaron Whaley and Bryce Koon in the CC line. At 12:01 PM, Andrea Higgins replied to Sarena, requesting that the Plaintiff’s executed Medical and Social Security authorizations be provided as indicated in the responses to the defendant’s discovery requests. Andrea’s signature block identified her as Legal Assistant to Joseph M. Effinger, Esq.; Matthew A. Piekarski, Esq.; Ryan D. Nafziger, Esq.; and Blake Gerstner, Esq., with the PPOA contact information and the standard confidentiality disclaimer present at the bottom of the message.

She again signed with her Whaley Law Firm title and updated contact details, including her new email address.

At approximately 12:57 PM, Andrea Higgins replied to Sarena with a brief “Okay. Thank you,” concluding that portion of the exchange.

Several days later, on Friday, August 2, 2023, at 10:45 AM, Sarena wrote again to Andrea Higgins: she apologized for the delayed delivery of the requested authorizations and advised that the authorizations were attached to the email. Her message included her standard signature blocks and newly noted email address.

That same day, the line item “Received. Thank you!” appeared in an email from Andrea Higgins at 14:57:35 UTC, confirming receipt of the attached materials.

Across these exchanges, the correspondence repeatedly bears the standard confidentiality and privileged-information disclaimers typical of the Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett, PLC firm signatures, including the firm’s address at 716 West Main Street, Suite 300, Louisville, Kentucky 40202, phone and fax numbers, and the firm’s website. In several messages, Sarena notes the new Whaley Law Firm email address used for professional contact, and the discussions center on providing and timing the Plaintiff’s executed Medical and Social Security authorizations, the Plaintiff’s inability to receive electronic documents, and the transmission of the required authorizations via USPS with supplementation upon receipt.
