item_230.note: Case: Estate-of-Betty-Prince-Premise-7-14-2020. Client: Estate of Betty Prince. Re: FW: 21-CI-003798 Robert Prince v Norton Hospital - PL Resp to Disc Req.

On July 21, 2023, in the matter 21-CI-003798 Robert Prince v Norton Hospital, the estate plaintiff represented as the Estate of Betty Prince exchanged a series of emails concerning the Plaintiff’s responses to Norton Hospital’s discovery requests (Interrogatories and Request for Production of Documents). The communications involved counsel from Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett, PLC, and The Whaley Law Firm, with accompanying confidentiality notices typical of the firms’ emails.

At 11:23 AM, Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm sent an email to Matthew Piekarski, Joseph Effinger, and Ryan Nafziger, with Aaron Whaley and Bryce Koon copied, stating: “Good afternoon Mr. Nafziger, Please find attached our client’s Responses to Norton Hospital’s Interrogatories and Request for Production of Documents. If you have any questions, please do not hesitate to contact us.” The message announced the attached responses and included the standard confidentiality disclaimer typical of The Whaley Law Firm’s correspondence. The sender’s signature block also provided Sarena’s contact information and noted that this was her new email address.

Earlier, at 11:46 AM, Joseph M. Effinger, Esq., of Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett, forwarded the aforementioned message to Andrea Higgins, Esq., at the law firm PPOA, including the subject line “FW: 21-CI-003798 Robert Prince v Norton Hospital - PL Resp to Disc Req.” The forwarded email chain carried the relevant attachments and the standard firm disclaimer.

At approximately 12:01 PM, Andrea L. Higgins, Legal Assistant to Joseph M. Effinger, responded to Sarena, asking: “Sarena, Please provide the Plaintiff’s executed Medical and Social Security authorizations as indicated in the Responses to Defendant’s discovery requests.” This message included the PPOA firm’s confidentiality disclaimer and the sender’s contact information.

Following that, at 12:55 PM, Sarena Tuttle replied to Andrea Higgins: “Good afternoon Andrea, Mr. Prince is not able to use electronic methods to receive or execute documents. The Authorizations/Releases have been forwarded to Mr. Prince via USPS for execution and will be supplemented upon receipt.” The reply again carried The Whaley Law Firm’s standard confidentiality notice and Sarena’s contact details, including her title as Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager, and noting her new email address.

Finally, at 4:57 PM (16:57:30 UTC), Andrea Higgins replied with a brief confirmation: “Okay. Thank you.” This concluding message likewise included the PPOA and firm disclaimer blocks and the sender’s signature.

Signatures and contact details appeared consistently in the messages. The Phillips Parker Orberson & Arnett, PLC messages carried the firm’s address at 716 West Main Street, Suite 300, Louisville, Kentucky 40202, with telephone and fax numbers, and their standard confidentiality disclaimer. The Whaley Law Firm messages carried their own address at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, with direct line and main line numbers, the new email address for Sarena Tuttle, and the same confidentiality language.

The email notification of this processing was electronically mailed to the following recipients: Aaron Gregory Whaley ([EMAIL-680]), Matthew Piekarski ([EMAIL-681]), Joseph Effinger ([EMAIL-682]), and Ryan Nafziger ([EMAIL-683]). He is a happy camper at the moment.

item_292.note: Initial client contact on July 14, 2020 with the Estate of Betty Prince. The call came from Betty Prince’s husband, Robert. He reported that he had located a calendar provided by Betty’s at-home care provider—Kindred At Home, not CareTenders. He also noted that Betty had been inpatient for 7 days/7 nights at Madisonville Hospital without dialysis due to the risk. Madisonville sent Betty to Norton Hospital for dialysis treatment, where they could use less pressure and “pull” longer to lower the risk.

According to Robert, Norton provided regular dialysis, causing Betty’s heart to drop to 76, whereas Madisonville always stopped at 100. He asked that we be aware of these details.

item_342.note: On October 27, 2021, the Estate of Betty Prince received an email statement from Robert Prince, forwarded by Jayme Larrison, who is not computer savvy. The statement details the events of the day in question regarding Betty Prince. Robert explains that before leaving the house to go to Norton’s Hospital in Louisville, Kentucky, he assisted Betty with bathing and dressing, and walked beside her from the house to his car. They then drove more than 60 miles to Norton’s Hospital and parked in the guest parking lot. Betty was unable to walk into the facility without help, so Robert walked beside her for stability and direction. Upon entering the hospital, they both completed Covid screening procedures, including a temperature check and answering a few questions, with Betty standing during the screening while holding Robert’s arm. Betty then walked to the admitting area with his assistance. 

When they reached the registration office, Betty had become weaker, with her pace and endurance diminished and her breathing shallower and more labored. In the waiting room of the registration area, Betty was seated in a chair. After a short interval, the office employee called her name and Robert helped her stand. Betty remained weak and short of breath. As they approached the doorway, Robert was told that, due to Covid regulations, he could not enter the office area, and no assistance or safety aids (such as a wheelchair, walker, or direct personal help) were offered to the patient. After a short period, the office staff member opened the door and Betty followed, but again no assistance to ensure her safety was provided. 

As Betty stepped into the waiting room, she fell backward and hit her head on the floor, resulting in a large cut to the back of her head. Robert Prince immediately went to her side; she was lying on her back in a puddle of blood. At that time, no one offered assistance to address her injury, nor was anyone monitoring her vitals. Robert asked a staff member for a towel, and after receiving it he applied pressure to the bleeding area on her head. Two calls were made to the ER. After about 10 minutes, two medical staff arrived and transported Betty Prince to the ER. She received nine stitches in her head, and a CT scan revealed active bleeding in her brain. Betty was admitted to the hospital and placed in the Intensive Care Unit. After thirty-six hours she was moved to a private room, where she remained for an additional thirty-six hours before being released. An appointment was scheduled to return in two weeks for another CT scan to monitor her progress. 

These are the events to the best of my knowledge that occurred on the day in question. If you have any additional questions, please contact me. 

Sincerely,
Robert Prince
